<div id="review_177630514" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177630514" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177630514?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177630514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4016424135897318371">The writing is <u>very</u> descriptive up to the point of being tedious but that’s fine because the plot’s simple enough to follow: Alex is not a good kid. He is a bully and a thief. His life of petty crime changes once he is sent to the Furnace. Now consider the tag line: <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Beneath Heaven is Hell. Beneath Hell is Furnace. </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Scary? Yes? No? If this were one’s first foray into the world of YA horror/thriller (or whatever genre Lockdown can be classified under,) I definitely say yes. But is it sad that I</span>
  <span id="freeText4016424135897318371" style="display:none">The writing is <u>very</u> descriptive up to the point of being tedious but that’s fine because the plot’s simple enough to follow: Alex is not a good kid. He is a bully and a thief. His life of petty crime changes once he is sent to the Furnace. Now consider the tag line: <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Beneath Heaven is Hell. Beneath Hell is Furnace. </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Scary? Yes? No? If this were one’s first foray into the world of YA horror/thriller (or whatever genre Lockdown can be classified under,) I definitely say yes. But is it sad that I didn’t find it as scary as I was hoping? It’s not like Lockdown isn’t bloody, gory or violent ~ it’s all of those things. Are child labor, gang killings, skinless bloodthirsty dogs, men with gas masks permanently sewn onto their faces and a warden that may or may not be the devil himself, not scary enough? Have I been desensitized? Or maybe it’s that the descriptions got in my way.<br /><br />It isn’t a girly book either with the happy absence of a romance; rather it’s focused on survival, escape... and friendship. Alex, well what can I say? He did/ does some dumb stuff but is relatable nonetheless. Who wouldn’t want to escape from the hell hole he’d found himself in. All the kids wanted out and their reactions were all very real… as in pee your pants, cry in your sleep and scream, kind of real. Surprisingly there were funny moments, especially from Zee. I love that kid!<br /><br />It’s dark and it's descriptive(good thing? bad thing? you decide...) <br /><br /><b>3/5</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4016424135897318371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1332027144" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11295257639105195684">Fast paced and bloody brilliant.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Don't go looking for snakes, you might find them..<br/>Don't send your eyes to the sun, you might blind them,<br/>Haven't I seen you here before?<br/>There ain't no heroes here....”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437941997ra/15649197.gif' width='304' height='221' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is a shit-meet-fan kind of book.   <span id="freeText11295257639105195684" style="display:none">Fast paced and bloody brilliant.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Don't go looking for snakes, you might find them..<br>Don't send your eyes to the sun, you might blind them,<br>Haven't I seen you here before?<br>There ain't no heroes here....”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437941997ra/15649197.gif" width="304" height="221" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is a shit-meet-fan kind of book. There are no sugary bits glossing over events because of the main character's age. It's actually adds to the horror, when you are forced to see kids as adults and surviving trough ordeals you are certain most adults wouldn't survive trough.<br><br>It has it all. Underground prison from hell, gangs and turf war. Fights, murder, mad science experiments and a band of unlikely friends. <br><br>I have been reading quite a lot of dystopia lately and can safely say that I still have the taste for it. I like the fact that it's a rich genre. This particular spin is very engaging, it doesn't leave you with two minutes to catch your breath. It keeps you on your toes all the time. It's not something for the fans of insta justice, and evil vs. good. <br><br>This book will give you chills....<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437941800ra/15649177.gif" width="304" height="179" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_930275058" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/930275058" />
    <a title="Cindy Newton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6082517-cindy-newton"><img alt="Cindy Newton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432075684p2/6082517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/930275058?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy Newton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy Newton" href="/user/show/6082517-cindy-newton">Cindy Newton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=ya-books-read">ya-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer930275058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16563027394534615921">This book is the first in a series of five altogether, and it starts off with a bang. Society has devolved into a place where there is no quarter given for age in the consideration of a crime, and young children (pre-teens) are imprisoned--for life--in maximum security facilities for serious crimes. The main character, Alex, and his friend Toby, are busted ripping off a house. This is a problem for them, but the even bigger problem is that they are not caught by the police--that would have been </span>
  <span id="freeText16563027394534615921" style="display:none">This book is the first in a series of five altogether, and it starts off with a bang. Society has devolved into a place where there is no quarter given for age in the consideration of a crime, and young children (pre-teens) are imprisoned--for life--in maximum security facilities for serious crimes. The main character, Alex, and his friend Toby, are busted ripping off a house. This is a problem for them, but the even bigger problem is that they are not caught by the police--that would have been a good day. Instead, it is a mysterious set of menacing men who frame Alex for a much worse crime than burglary. He finds himself, in short order, imprisoned in the worst of all prisons--Furnace. Supposedly inescapable, the youngsters condemned to spend their lives there are all but written off as dead by society. Civil rights? Visiting hours? They don't exist in Furnace. The fight for survival from the usual prison ills is present: sadistic guards, prison gangs, suffocating hopelessness. But wait! Furnace has a whole other level of terrors awaiting its inmates. Who are these mysterious gas-masked creatures roaming the cell-blocks? What's wrong with the guards' eyes? And what's up with those weird dogs? <br /><br />These and other questions will NOT be answered in this book--that's for future books in the series. There are plenty of chills and thrills in this book, however, even if you don't completely understand what's going on. The action is fast-paced, the prose pretty spare, and the somewhat claustrophobic atmosphere is well-conveyed. The only characters I have any real interest in at this point are Alex and his cell-mate, Donovan, but I hope that will change as the series continues. I am eager to find out the answers to the above questions, as well as find out what happens from the pretty massive cliff-hanger that this book ended on. All in all, an engrossing read and an unusual premise. I'm definitely going on to the next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16563027394534615921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1031794741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17763851054164774325">Action packed Young Adult Sci-Fi/Dystopia/Horror/Thriller <br/><br/>The pros:<br/>* This is my first time to read this writers work, and I have to say, I really like the writing style<br/>* This was an intense read - I think my 12 year old will enjoy this one just as much as I did (even though this book had a horror feel to it, the language was relatively clean, and there was no sex etc.) - it never felt geared towards young adults. It's just one of those books that a wide variety of readers will enjoy.<br/><br/><br/>The cons:<br/>* Q</span>
  <span id="freeText17763851054164774325" style="display:none">Action packed Young Adult Sci-Fi/Dystopia/Horror/Thriller <br /><br />The pros:<br />* This is my first time to read this writers work, and I have to say, I really like the writing style<br />* This was an intense read - I think my 12 year old will enjoy this one just as much as I did (even though this book had a horror feel to it, the language was relatively clean, and there was no sex etc.) - it never felt geared towards young adults. It's just one of those books that a wide variety of readers will enjoy.<br /><br /><br />The cons:<br />* Quite pricey - I paid $7.80 for this on Amazon (it's only a 280 pages) and it's not even loanable<br />* The ending pissed me off - I'm just not a fan of cliffhanger endings<br /><br />Upon completion, I am a bit disappointed. I guess because when I pay this much for a book, I like a little more in the sense of closure when I'm finished. I'm still likely to continue on to the next book in this series at a later date though. I'm just not feeling overly eager to jump into at this time.<br /><br />UPDATE: After checking out some reviews on the other 4 books in this series, I have decided not to continue this one because of these reasons: Each book is insanely overpriced; They all seem to end with brutal cliffhangers; the blurbs all sound too familiar......he plans escape, gets caught, starts all over. Nah, Im out. This was a pretty decent read, but Im just not intrigued enough to personally continue it.<br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1P0xgW/V5szpJADdwpKMK0P0CPwt9G7H8Kk+tYS5JNenwZZHlOsth6yqxUpqNbS6hBswlXfk9er991qdr3Ieqw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uyi2xAOwzPN+ajv8UYUZLuceEbSWOTPmpKSYkge2BjvIFBEC+I4HuDvk/mv5IiG/IPEp3cwpqMup+vy6LH08Rw==')})
  }

          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8308877152844489740">Alexander Gordon Smith is the author of the Escape from Furnace series of young adult novels, including <i>Lockdown</i> and <i>Solitary</i>. Born in 1979 in Norwich, England, he always wanted to be a writer. After experimenting in the service and retail trades for a few years, Smith decided to go to University. He studied English and American Literature at the University of East Anglia, and it was here that he </span>
  <span id="freeText8308877152844489740" style="display:none">Alexander Gordon Smith is the author of the Escape from Furnace series of young adult novels, including <i>Lockdown</i> and <i>Solitary</i>. Born in 1979 in Norwich, England, he always wanted to be a writer. After experimenting in the service and retail trades for a few years, Smith decided to go to University. He studied English and American Literature at the University of East Anglia, and it was here that he first explored his love of publishing. Along with poet Luke Wright, he founded Egg Box Publishing, a groundbreaking magazine and press that promotes talented new authors. He also started writing literally hundreds of articles, short stories and books ranging from Scooby Doo comic strips to world atlases, Midsomer Murders to X-Files. The endless research for these projects led to countless book ideas germinating in his head. His first book, The Inventors, written with his nine-year-old brother Jamie, was published in the U.K. in 2007. He lives in England.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/alexandergordonsmith">http://us.macmillan.com/author/alexan...</a></span>
